+Jamison Brereton

32 (548)
Indra
Vasiс╣гс╣нha Maitr─Бvaruс╣Зi (1тАУ25), ┼Ъakti V─Бsiс╣гс╣нha (26ab), Vasiс╣гс╣нha or ┼Ъakti V─Бsiс╣гtha (26cdтАУ27)
27 verses: br╠еhat─л alternating with satobr╠еhat─л, except dvipad─Б vir─Бj 3, arranged in prag─Бthas
This final hymn in the VIIth Maс╣Зс╕Нala Indra cycle is a loose collection of prag─Бthas, the first of which has a two-p─Бda extension (vs. 3). Even within the verse pairs there is little cohesion. But there is a unifying theme that runs throughout: IndraтАЩs gener ous giving and our grateful receiving, to an extent unusual even in an Indra hymn. Moreover, it is not only IndraтАЩs giving that we seek: it is repeatedly emphasized that Indra helps and gives to mortals who themselves give, that is, the patrons of the sacrifice (see, e.g., vss. 7, 8, 10, 15).
The hymn opens (vs. 1) with the preoccupation that has been visible in many Indra hymns in VII, the fear that rival sacrificers may attract Indra to their own rituals, and IndraтАЩs epithet тАЬinvoked by manyтАЭ appears several times (vss. 17, 20, 26). Much of the hymn is concerned with defining the type of ritual behavior that will cause Indra to choose one sacrifice over another.
Indra is supreme in this hymn. In its twenty-seven verses there is only one men tion of another divinity, the Maruts in verse 10.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬLet not, Indra, (other) worshippers detain you far from us; come from whatever distance to ourassembly; present at this ceremony, hear our (prayers).тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

Let not (any other) cantors at all stop you at a distance from us.
Even from afar come here to our joint revelry, or being (already) here hearken (to us),

+Griffith

LET none, no, not thy worshippers, delay thee far away from us.
Even from far away come thou unto our feast, or listen if already here.

+Geldner

Auch andere S├дnger sollen dich ja nicht fern von uns anhalten. Auch aus der Ferne komme zu unserem Opfergelage, oder wenn du hier bist, so h├╢re zu!

+Grassmann

Dich m├╢gen selbst die Beter nicht zum Stillstand bringen fern von uns; Auch aus der Ferne komm zu unserm Mahle her, wenn hier du bist, so h├╢re uns.

+Elizarenkova

+Jamison Brereton Notes

sud├бkс╣гiс╣Зa- is a triple pun. In its only other RVic occurrence (VIII.33.5) it means тАШhaving a good right (horse)тАЩ, but it could equally mean тАШhaving a good right (hand)тАЩ, alluding to the immediately preceding v├бjrahasta- тАШhaving the mace in his handтАЩ. And, in keeping with the theme of giving, it can refer to the d├бkс╣гiс╣З─Б-, the priestly giftтАЩ distributed at the dawn sacrifice. This would respond to the r─Бy├бsk─Бma- тАШdesirous of wealthтАЩ, which opens the verse.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬMay Indra, whose ear is ready to hear, listen to the suppliant for riches, and never disappoint ourprayers; he who is the giver of hundreds and thousands; may no one ever hinder him when willing to give.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

He will listen: he of listening ears is implored for goods. He will never neglect our songs.
The one who just in a single day will give hundreds, thousandsтАФno one will confound him when he is about to give.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

Geldner joins c with b, rather than d as I do. This is possible, but the topic of giving in both c and d connects them thematically.

+Griffith

May he whose ear is open hear us. He is asked for wealth: will he despise our prayer?
Him who bestows at once a hundred thousand gifts none shall restrain when he would give.

+Geldner

Er h├╢re; h├╢renden Ohres wird er um Sch├дtze angegangen. Niemals solle er unsere Lobreden verschm├дhen, der sogar auf einmal Tausende, Hunderte schenkt. Keiner soll ihn hindern, wenn er schenken will.

+Grassmann

Mit offnem Ohre h├╢r’ er, wenn um Gut wir flehn, und achte unsrer Lieder stets; Ihn, der auf einmal hunderttausend G├╝ter schenkt; ihn, wenn er gibt, h├дlt niemand auf.

+Elizarenkova

English translation:

+Jamison Brereton

Press soma for soma-drinking Indra who holds the mace.
Cook cooked dishes. Just cause (him) to help. It is only the generous giver who is a joy to the one who generously gives.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

├бvase kс╣Ыс╣Зudhvam is close to a periphrastic causative, since тАЬmake [=create] (him) for helpтАЭ is unlikely to take the long-created Indra as object. Zehnder (p. 7 and passim) takes it as such.

+Griffith

For Indra, Soma-drinker, armed with thunder, press the Soma juice.
Make ready your dressed meats: cause him to favour us. The Giver blesses him who gives.

+Geldner

Presset dem Somatrinker den Soma, dem Indra, der die Keule hat! Kochet Kochspeisen; machet zur Gnade geneigt! Nur der Freigebige ist dem Freigebigen eine Freude.

+Grassmann

Dem Somatrinker Indra presst den Soma, ihm, der Blitze tr├дgt; Die Br├╝hen br├╝ht, zur H├╝lfe schafft ihn auch herbei, der Labsal schenkt dem schenkenden.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬOfferers of the libation, do not hesitate; be active; sacrifice to the mighty benefactor for the sake ofriches; the assiduous worshipper conquers (his enemies), dwells in a habitation, and prospers; the gods favournot the imperfect rite.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Na dev─Бsaс╕е karatnave: karatnuс╕е = kutsita kriya, bad or defective act of religion; men donot become gods by such means, dev─Б na bhavanti

+Jamison Brereton

You pressers of soma, do not fail; be skillful for the great one. Make (him inclined) to thrust wealth (to us).
It is just the surpassing man who wins: he dwells peacefully, he thrives. The gods are not for the petty.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

kс╣Ыс╣Зudhv├бm тАж ─Бt├║je similarly functions as a periphrastic causative. So also Zehnder (p. 20 and passim).

+Griffith

Grudge not, ye Soma pourers; stir you, pay the rites, for wealth, to the great Conqueror.
Only the active conquers dwells in peace, and thrives: not for the niggard are the Gods.

+Geldner

Bleibt nicht Stecken, ihr Somavollen, machet es dem Gro├Яen recht! Machet, da├Я er Reichtum herausschlage. Nur der Meister gewinnt das Spiel; er wohnt gl├╝cklich, gedeiht. Die G├╢tter sind nicht f├╝r den St├╝mper.

+Grassmann

Nicht opfert fehl, o Priester, macht’s dem grossen recht, zur Reichthumsgabe regt ihn an; Wer eifrig ist, der siegt, hat Frieden und gedeiht; dem Kargen sind die G├╢tter feind.

+Elizarenkova

The man whom Indra and the Marut host defend comes to a stable full of kine.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬWhat mortal, Indra, injures him who has you for his support? He who offers you (sacrificial) food,Maghavan, with faith, he obtains food on the day of the libation.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

P─Бrye divi v─Бj─л v─Бjam siс╣г─Бsati = sautyeahani sa haviс╣гm─Бn annam sevate

+Jamison Brereton

What mortal will dare against him who has you as his
possession, Indra?
It is with trust in you, bounteous one, that on the decisive day the one vying for the prize seeks to win the prize.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

┼Ыraddh─Б╠Бis most likely instrumental, but its lack of contraction with the following vowel in the Saс╣Гhit─Б text gives pause. See Oldenberg on this problem. 36 v─Бj─л╠Бv─Б╠Бjaс╣Г siс╣г─Бsati seems like a variant of g├бmad v─Б╠Бjam v─Бj├бyan in 11a with different emphasis. See also 20a below.

+Griffith

Indra, what mortal will attack the man who hath his wealth in thee?
The strong will win the spoil on the decisive day through faith in thee, O Maghavan.

+Geldner

Welcher Sterbliche, o Indra, wagt sich an den, der dich besitzt? Im Vertrauen auf dich, du Gabenreicher, sucht am entscheidenden Tage der Preisk├дmpfer den Siegerpreis zu gewinnen.

+Grassmann

Welch Sterblicher, o Indra, kann dem dir ergebnen Schaden thun? Wer dir vertraut, o m├дchtiger, am Tag der Schlacht, gewinnet Beute, beutereich.

+Elizarenkova

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬAnimate (those men) for the destruction of their foes, who offer treasures which are dear to you, theabounder in wealth; may we, lord of bay steeds, along with (your) worshippers, pass over all difficulties by yourguidance.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

At the smashing of obstacles spur on the bounteous ones who give their own dear goods.
O you of the fallow bays, with your guidance may we, along with our patrons, overcome all difficulties.

+Griffith

In battles with the foe urge on our mighty ones who give the treasures dear to thee,
And may we with our princes, Lord of Tawny Steeds! pass through all peril, led by thee.

+Geldner

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬYours, Indra, is the vast valuable wealth; you cherish the middling; you rule over all that which is themost precious; no one opposes you in (the recovering of the) cattle.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Na kis’ tva goс╣гu vriс╣Зvate = goс╣гu nimitteс╣гuke api tv─Бm na v─Бrayanti, none resist or oppose you on account of the cows

+Jamison Brereton

Yours alone is the lowest good thing, Indra; you prosper the middling one.
You rule over each highest one entirely. No one obstructs you when cattle (are at stake).

+Griffith

Thine, Indra, is the lowest wealth, thou cherishest the mid-most wealth,
Thou ever rulest all the highest: in the fray for cattle none resisteth thee.

+Geldner

Dein, Indra, ist das unterste Gut, du mehrest das mittlere, du gebietest ├╝ber alles h├╢chste insgesamt. Nicht wehren sie dir im Kampf um die Rinder.

+Grassmann

Das untre Gut ist, Indra, dein; das mittlere entfaltest du; Und ├╝ber alles obere gebietest du; dich hemmt man nicht, wenn’s Heerden gilt.

+Elizarenkova

рд╕рд╛рдпрдг-рднрд╛рд╖реНрдпрдореН

рд╣реЗ рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░ рддреНрд╡рдВ рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡рд╕реНрдп рд╕рд░реНрд╡рд╕реНрдп рд╕реНрддреЛрддреБрд░реНрдпрдЬрдорд╛рдирд╕реНрдп рд╡рд╛ рдзрдирджрд╛рдГ рдзрдирд╕реНрдп рджрд╛рддрд╛ рд╕рдиреН рд╢реНрд░реБрддрдГ рдкреНрд░рд╕рд┐рджреНрдзрдГ рдЕрд╕рд┐ред рдп рдИрдВ рдп рдПрддреЗ рдЖрдЬрдпрдГ рдпреБрджреНрдзрд╛рдирд┐ рднрд╡рдиреНрддрд┐ рддреЗрд╖реНрд╡рдкрд┐ рдзрдирджрд╛рдГ рд╢реНрд░реБрддреЛрд╜рд╕рд┐ ред рд╣реЗ рдкреБрд░реБрд╣реВрдд рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡рдГ рд╕рд░реНрд╡реЛрд╜рдкрд┐ рдЕрдпрдВ рдкрд╛рд░реНрдерд┐рд╡рдГ рдЬрдирдГ рддрд╡ ред рддреНрд╡рддреНрдд рдЗрддреНрдпрд░реНрдердГред рдЕрд╡рд╕реНрдпреБрдГ рд░рдХреНрд╖рд╛рдорд┐рдЪреНрдЫрдиреН рдирд╛рдо рдЕрдиреНрдирдореБрджрдХрдВ рд╡рд╛ ред тАШрдмрд░реНрд╣рд┐рдГ рдирд╛рдо’ рдЗрддреНрдпреБрджрдХрдирд╛рдорд╕реБ рдкрд╛рдард╛рддреН ред рднрд┐рдХреНрд╖рддреЗ рдпрд╛рдЪрддреЗ ред рддреНрд╡рд╛рдореЗрд╡реЗрддрд┐ рд╢реЗрд╖рдГ рее

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬYou are celebrated as the giver of wealth to all even where battles occur; all the people of theearth–desirous of protection, solicit you, the invoked of many.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Dhanad─Б asi ┼Ыruto ya ─лm bhavantyaj─Бyaс╕е = yeete ─Бjayo yuddh─Бni bhavanti teс╣гu api dhanad─Бс╕е ┼Ыrutosi

+Jamison Brereton

You are famed as the giver of spoils to everyone, whenever there are (battle-)drives.
Every earth-dweller here, when seeking help, desires a share in your name, o you who are invoked by many.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

The relative clause of b, y├б ─лm bh├бvanti ─Бj├бyaс╕е, is very peculiar. There is no possible referent for the y├й in either the preceding or the following main clause, and in addition the ─лm lacks function. It seems like a mangled paraphrase of I.81.3 y├бd ud─л╠Бrata ─Бj├бyaс╕е тАЬwhen (battle-)drives arise/happen,тАЭ but what caused the mangling is unclear to me. The y├й can be by тАЬattractionтАЭ to the m. nom. pl. ─Бj├бyaс╕е from putative *y├бd, and this set of Indra hymns has several examples of functionless ─лm (VII.20.3, 21.1). But it still lacks motivation.

The VP n─Б╠Бma bhikс╣гate тАЬdesires a share in your nameтАЭ is striking and a little puzzling. The same phrase n─Б╠Бma тИЪbhaj is found in V.57.5, but there it means that the Maruts, the subjects of the verb, all share the same name. Here, by contrast, it must be a clever way of saying that everyone calls IndraтАЩs name, a novel paraphrase of the common epithet of Indra puruh┼лt├б- тАШcalled upon by manyтАЩ, found in this verse and vss. 20 and 26. (The English slang equivalent would be тАЬwants a piece of you.тАЭ) Geldner renders n─Б╠Бma bhikс╣гate as тАЬDeinen Namen fleht тАж anтАЭ (implores), robbing the expression of its vividness.

+Griffith

Thou art renowned as giving wealth to every one in all the battles that are fought.
Craving protection, all these people of the earth, O Much-invoked, implore thy name.

+Geldner

Du bist als der Geber jeglichen Schatzes ber├╝hmt, was es auch f├╝r K├дmpfe gibt. Deinen Namen fleht jeder schutzbed├╝rftige Erdenbewohner hier an, du Vielgerufener.

+Grassmann

Ber├╝hmter Geber bist du jedes Kampfgewinns, wie viel der K├дmpfe auch entstehn; Und deinen Namen, vielgerufner, ruft allhier voll H├╝lfsbegier der Erdenmensch.

+Elizarenkova

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬIf I were lord of as much (affluence) as you are, Indra, then might I support (your) worshippers,dispenser of wealth, and not squander it upon wickedness.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

If I were lord of as much as you are, Indra,
I would seek to make just my praiser (well) set up, you excavator of goods; I would not give him over to ill-estate.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

The root тИЪ─л┼Ы overwhelmingly takes the gen.; the construction here is identified by Grassmann (s.v. ─л┼Ы, col. 236: #8 mit dem Acc.) as mixed: the gen. y─Б╠Бvataс╕е is construed with the implied 2nd ps. тАЬas much as you are lord overтАЭ (y─Б╠Бvatas tv├бm [─л╠Б┼Ыiс╣гe]) in p─Бda a, which is picked up by the acc. et─Б╠Бvad in the contrary-to-fact тАЬif I were lord over so muchтАЭ (y├бd тАж et─Б╠Бvad ah├бm ─л╠Б┼Ыiya). I think it more likely that et─Б╠Бvad here is a quasi-adverbial summing up of the dependent clause; a more literal tr. would be тАЬif I were lord to such an extent asтАЭ or the like. The other passages assembled under GrassmannтАЩs #8 can be variously explained and do not provide strong evidence for an alternative case frame with тИЪ─л┼Ы. In III.18.3 y─Б╠Бvad is again adverbial; see the published translation тАЬinasmuch as I am master тАжтАЭ In VIII.68.7 ─л╠Б┼Ыe is properly construed with a gen. (kс╣Ыс╣гс╣н─лn─Б╠Бm) in its own p─Бda; the acc. cited by Grassmann, p┼лrvy─Б╠Бm ├бnuс╣гс╣нutim in the previous p─Бda, is probably an acc. of respect (see comm. ad loc.) For nearby VII.37.7 as well as III.51.4, the latter cited only as a possibility by Grassmann, see comm. ad locc.

+Griffith

If I, O Indra, were the Lord of riches ample as thine own,
I should support the singer, God. who givest wealth! and not abandon him to woe.

+Grassmann

Wenn, Indra, ich so viel des Guts bes├дsse, wie dir eigen ist, Dem S├дnger theilt ich reichlich zu, o G├╝terquell, nicht g├дb’ ich ihn dem Elend hin.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬMay I daily distribute wealth to the venerable wherever abiding; no other, Maghavan, than you is to besought by us; (no other is to us) a most excellent protector.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

for there exists no other, better friendship for us than you, nor even a father, bounteous one.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬA man acquires not wealth by unbecoming praise; affluence devolves not upon one obstructing(sacrifice) in you, Maghavan, is the power whereby bounty (may be shown) to such as I am on the day of libation.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

Not by a bad(ly made) praise does a mortal find goods, nor will wealth reach the one who fails.
ItтАЩs an easy skill for you, bounteous oneтАФgiving to the likes of me on the decisive day.

+Griffith

A moral wins no riches by unworthy praise: wealth comes not to the niggard churl.
Light is the task to give, O Maghavan, to one like me on the decisive day.

+Geldner

Nicht findet ein Sterblicher durch schlechtes Loblied Gut, nicht kommt der Reichtum zu dem, der stecken bleibt. F├╝r dich, du G├╢nner, ist es eine Leichtigkeit, meinesgleichen an dem entscheidenden Tage zu schenken.

+Grassmann

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Like udders: adugdha iva dhenavo = we praiseyou as unmilked kine praise their calves; the fullness of ladles, yath─Б dhenavaс╕е kс╣гirap┼лrс╣Зodhastvenavartante tad vat somap┼лrс╣Зa camastvena vartam─Бn─Б vayam bhс╣Ы┼Ыam abhiс╣г– umaс╕е, as the cows remain withthe state of the udders being full of milk, so we, abiding with the state of the ladle full of Soma, glorify you; Yajuс╣г27.35

+Jamison Brereton Notes

Despite GeldnerтАЩs easy тАЬdessen Auge die Sonne ist,тАЭ I cannot accept this for svardс╣Ы╠Б┼Ыam. First, dс╣Ы╠Б┼Ы- is never an тАШeyeтАЩ, but rather тАШseeingтАЩ or тАШhaving the appearance ofтАЩ, and furthermore, itтАЩs Varuс╣Зa who has the sun as his eye (that is, his spy). Here I think the point is rather that Indra, like the sun, sees everything in the world, here expressed by the merism тАЬthe moving and the still.тАЭ

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬNo other such as you are, celestial or terrestrial, has been or will be born; desirous of horses, of food,of cattle affluent Indra, we invoke you.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

There is no other heavenly one like you, nor earthly; neither born, nor to be born.
Seeking horses, seeking cows, vying for the prize, we call upon you, bounteous Indra.

+Griffith

None other like to thee, of earth or of the heavens, hath been or ever will be born.
Desiring horses, Indra Maghavan! and kine, as men of might we call on thee.

+Geldner

Kein anderer Himmlischer oder Irdischer ist dir gleich geboren oder wird geboren werden. Nach Rossen, nach Rindern verlangend rufen wir Preisk├дmpfer dich, du gabenreicher Indra.

+Grassmann

Kein andrer ist im Himmel, auf der Erd’ wie du gewesen nicht, noch wird er sein; Nach Ross und Rind verlangend flehn wir, Indra, dich, o reicher, Opfer bringend an.

+Elizarenkova

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬElder Indra, bring that (wealth to me), being the junior, for, Maghavan, you have from the beginningbeen possessed of infinite treasure, and are to be adored at repeated sacrifices.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

Bring this greater (good) here, Indra, to those who are lesser, for you, bounteous one, are from of old one with many goods, and the one to be called upon at every raid.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

There are two word plays in this verse. The simpler one is between the impv. bhara тАШbringтАЩ in p─Бda a and the ─Бmreс╕Нita bh├бre-bhare тАШat every raidтАЩ, where the noun bh├бra- has been specialized from тАШ(an occasion for) bearing awayтАЩ to тАШraidтАЩ.

The more complex one involves the creation and disappointment of expectations. The verse begins with abh─л╠Бс╣гat├бс╕е. The juxtaposition of these two forms 37 (the latter being the pres. part. to тИЪas тАШbeтАЩ in either gen.-abl. sg. or acc. pl.) and their close sandhi, with retroflex initial с╣г, invites the audience to fill in the semantics of the lexeme abh├н тИЪas тАШbe superiorтАЩ. But to our surprise, at the end of this hemistich we find the semantic opposite, k├бn─лyasaс╕е тАШthe lesser onesтАЩ, requiring us to revise our analysis of the opening, dissolving the presumed lexeme into the directional preverb/preposition abh├н and the independent pres. participle modifying k├бn─лyasaс╕е much later in the line. For extensive discussion see Oldenberg

I cannot follow Grassmann, Oldenberg in interpreting jy─Б╠Бyaс╕е as voc., but take it, with Geldner, as neut. sg. with t├бd. Among other things, AiG III.296 notes only two masc. vocatives in -─лyas in the RV, this one and ├│j─лyaс╕е in X.120.4, which is also better taken as a neut.

+Griffith

Bring, Indra, the Victorious Ones; bring, elder thou, the younger host.
For, Maghavan, thou art rich in treasures from of old, and must be called in every fight.

+Geldner
